               Job Search: LinkedIns New Standalone App
              </span>
             </div>
             <div class="post-heading">
              <h1 class="post-title entry-title" itemprop="name headline">
               Job Search: LinkedIns New Standalone App
              </h1>
             </div>
             <div class="post-meta">
              <span class="post-author vcard">
               <i class="fa fa-user">
               </i>
               <span class="fn" itemprop="author" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
                <meta content="https://plus.google.com/107051614052586843330" itemprop="url"/>
                <a class="g-profile" href="https://plus.google.com/107051614052586843330" rel="author" title="author profile">
                 <span itemprop="name">
                  Shree Madhan
                 </span>
                </a>
               </span>
              </span>
              <span class="post-timestamp">
               <i class="fa fa-clock-o">
               </i>
               <meta content="http://www.softechnogeek.com/2014/06/job-search-linkedins-new-standalone-app.html" itemprop="url"/>
               <a class="timestamp-link" href="http://www.softechnogeek.com/2014/06/job-search-linkedins-new-standalone-app.html" rel="bookmark" title="permanent link">
                <abbr class="published timeago" itemprop="datePublished" title="2014-06-29T20:11:00+05:30">
                 Sunday, June 29, 2014
                </abbr>
               </a>
              </span>
              <span class="post-labels">
               <i class="fa fa-folder-open">
               </i>
               <a href="http://www.softechnogeek.com/search/label/Guest%20Post" rel="tag">
                Guest Post
               </a>
               ,
               <a href="http://www.softechnogeek.com/search/label/Social%20Media" rel="tag">
                Social Media
               </a>
              </span>
             </div>
            </div>
            <article>
             <div class="post-body entry-content" id="post-body-2064202358909922966" itemprop="articleBody">
              <meta content="   Lately, LinkedIn has reached new heights and become a leader in the job search space. This has be..." name="twitter:description"/>
              <table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" width="100%">
               <table align="center">
                <tr>
                 <td width="354">
                  <script async="" src="//pagead2.googlesyndication.com/pagead/js/adsbygoogle.js">
                  </script>
                  <!-- Medium Rectangle -->
                  <ins class="adsbygoogle" data-ad-client="ca-pub-9024475143075863" data-ad-slot="4756518236" style="display:inline-block;width:300px;height:250px">
                  </ins>
                  <script>
                   (adsbygoogle = window.adsbygoogle || []).push({});
                  </script>
                 </td>
                 <td>
                  <script id="mNCC" language="javascript">
                   medianet_width='300';  medianet_height= '250';  medianet_crid='446588150';
                  </script>
                  <script id="mNSC" language="javascript" src="http://contextual.media.net/nmedianet.js?cid=8CU158T4E">
                  </script>
                 </td>
                </tr>
               </table>
              </table>
              <div dir="ltr" style="text-align: left;" trbidi="on">
               <div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
                <a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-VC1uQmdssvg/U7AlD_k6CHI/AAAAAAAAFrI/GTdtC6n8hMY/s1600/LinkedIn-Standalone-app.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;">
                 <img alt="LinkedIn Standalone app" border="0" height="128" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-VC1uQmdssvg/U7AlD_k6CHI/AAAAAAAAFrI/GTdtC6n8hMY/s1600/LinkedIn-Standalone-app.jpg" title="LinkedIn Standalone app" width="200"/>
                </a>
               </div>
               Lately,
               <a href="http://www.softechnogeek.com/2012/12/New-TechCrunch-Social-Subscribe-Widget-For-Blogger.html" target="_blank">
                LinkedIn
               </a>
               has reached new heights and become a leader in the job search space. This has been due to their Talent Solutions offerings that have pulled in 275.9 million dollars within the first quarter of this year. To further their foothold, they have launched a new standalone job app for Apple iPhone, LinkedIn Job Search. This app is LinkedIns sixth standalone app and the fourth to be unveiled since the last 18 months. This latest app aims to help users find and apply for jobs.
               <a name="more">
               </a>
               <br/>
               <div>
                According to LinkedIn, about 40% of its 300 million users access the site on their smartphones. So, this is a step to attract users who access the site
                <a href="http://blog.cromaretail.com/index.php/now-thats-how-you-use-a-smartphone-this-is-just-brilliant/" rel="nofollow" target="_blank">
                 through smartphones
                </a>
                and tablets. This new LinkedIn app helps users sort out the listings by enabling them to filter by title, location, company, industry and seniority level.
                <br/>
                <br/>
                The recommendations for the
                <a href="http://www.softechnogeek.com/2013/01/Three-Adjustments-To-Create-Android-A-Bit-More-Quickly.html" target="_blank">
                 matching jobs
                </a>
                are provided to the users based on the saved searches and the jobs they have viewed. This app provides notifications even when the saved jobs are about to expire. It also gives notifications when a recruiter looks at the users application.
                <br/>
                <br/>
                LinkedIns new and
                <a href="http://www.softechnogeek.com/2014/05/how-to-launch-camera-app-quickly-on-android-by-twisting-your-hand.html" target="_blank">
                 amazing app
                </a>
                is created to make it easy for their users to search for a new job even while sitting at the desk of their current job. With the Job Search app, the users can easily filter the jobs based on seniority level, industry and location and save them to view in the future.
                <br/>
                <br/>
                This app is befitting for people who prefer to know whether the recruiters are looking at their applications. Currently, this
                <a href="http://www.softechnogeek.com/2014/06/automatically-turn-on-your-android-phone-by-just-picking-it-up.html" target="_blank">
                 app
                </a>
                is available only in the United States. However, LinkedIn has promised to provide its support in multiple languages worldwide.
               </div>
              </div>
